< text>
I took my cat Jeorgie in on Black Friday when almost no one else was available. My little brat had a fight with some other cat and came back with a huge bite mark on his hip.
The staff at Cottage  Pet Hospital were very helpful and the doctor laid out our options for us (use anti-biotics & wait OR do a surgery). She explained the pros and cons for each option  and gave us time to consider.
We chose go with the anti-biotics. The hospital called to check on Jeorgie  twice  and asked me questions in regards to his wound, to make sure the medication was working and its healing properly.

They also sent Jeorgie a card at the end of two weeks wishing him all the best.
So All in all an amazing place to take your pet. They really care about the animals that come into their clinic and are great at following up on your fur baby's health and recovery.< /text>

This has been an overdue review of our overall experience at The Cottage Pet Hospital.
Which has been a pleasant experience from the moment I picked up my phone to call and investigate pricings and booking an appointment. I was greeted by Liz , she took her time in answering all of my questions over the phone. She seemed calmed and pleasant and very informative.
My chihuahua had some type of paw allergies/rash. Being that we were first time customers they had to evaluate  her. It turned out to be  a common grass allergic reaction . She was given an injection that lasted a month and  since then it has cleared. She is due to  come back in soon, for the same reason. The cost of the consultation was reasonable.
Over all our experience was great. We arrrived and was finally able to meet Liz the girl I spoke with over the phone . And was  greeted  the same with the utmost respect and she was a pleasure. She took care of my Roxy!

I will be recommending this place to my friends and family . For all of their pet needs!<//review>

Pros are:
+ Dr. Sahai is wonderful and absolutely amazing at diagnosis while being practical about cost (aka without going into debt)
+ If you are upfront in a polite manner or are like me and super stressed when you pet is sick (and have a million questions), the nurses will do whatever they can to help
+ No appointments needed on weekends for shots, it's a quick and easy
+ (Most) of the staff seem to really love pets and care about their well-being! Our pets love people and bond with the staff when they are in for treatment, which we really love and puts us at ease

Cons:
- There is a sarcastic doctor here that we do not jive well with, we feel she is not as straightforward when we ask her questions and she will often joke to us about how she never brings in her pets to the vet and just lets stuff in their bodies "work out on their own" (how is that professional).

- They never remember my pet insurance covers flea medicine! Every time I come in and buy it, I have to pay full price and then get my insurance to work with Cottage Pet Hospital on proactively applying my discount and refunding me the rest. Pet Treatment: I brought my cat in for treatment after she started scooting across the carpet. Without getting into details the diagnosis was quick and treatment was effective.

Facility: There is a strong smell in this facility similar to most animal shelters I've been in. The staff do constantly clean but the building is dated and may have absorbed years of patient odors. I often see the staff cleaning and disinfecting after each patient and they are currently remodeling the facility so hopefully they will be able to reduce the smell.

Price: The prices for treatment seem comparable to that of Banfield Pet Hospitals found in most Petsmarts. They also seem to accept most insurance plans.

< name>
D Hart<//name>
< rating>
3< /rating>
<user>114811140324686405967<//user><GmapID>0x80e914771f7bce93:0x6c9422b52628cefa</GmapID>< review>
My husband and I just bought a house in Montecito and wanted to get our in-town gym lined up. We've had memberships to other private clubs everywhere we've lived, and wanted to see if SWELL was as good as some of our local friends said it was. We've learned to always ask current members what their experience is, and try out a week or so before buying a membership....mostly so that we don't get a membership and then constantly complain about it. We signed up separately and staggered our 3-day passes, to test the water of how the staff treated us, and if their sales pitches were different. Our overall experience was a mixed bag:

-Whoever is in charge of the pool chemicals is doing an excellent job--not overly chlorinated and no hair, bandaids, etc. floating around. We politely asked to share lanes with swimmers of similar speed, but there seemed to be a dramatic edge about territory that we're not accustomed to. We're used to masters swimmers who know how to shared lanes. It wasn't enough of an issue to annoy us, because we'll probably open water swim join local masters, anyway.
-We sat by the pool all 3 days we worked out, and were sandwiched in between a group of loud millennials playing music on their phones who said they weren't members but were just using the free 3-day pass to sit by the pool during a hot weekend...and several long time members who complained for a half hour about how a third of the lounge chairs had been missing for over a month, but not replaced yet by Scott. It indicated to us that the quality of the members is probably in decline--and the long time members are annoyed about it, and the non-members/new members are clueless about private club etiquette. I don't envy the drama management must have to put up at this time.
-Despite anti-harassment statements on the front of the pool locker room doors, I got hit on by two drunk guys in the hot tub who had their pitcher of beer sitting on the edge of the deck. Full on comments about my bikini before I even got settled in. Neither were members. That didn't happen when my husband was around...it's 2019, so no surprise there. Just wish that staff would cruise through once in a while and make sure that beer isn't on the edge of the pool, or guys getting drunk, or loud music playing, or towels laying all over the place.
-The front desk staff seemed to be generally stressed out, overworked, and annoyed at being asked to help with locker issues, juice bar requests, and membership questions. IMO, that annoyance seeped over to how members vs. non-members were treated.
-The biggest draw for us was the sheer number of equipment areas. We didn't have to wait for weight benches, machines, or padded spaces for basics like lunges. We could work out barefoot in some areas. The outdoor equipment over the pool is fantastic. The olympic lifting area was a huge plus for my husband, and plenty of TRX zones were great.
-I got zero sales pitches during or after the 3-day trial, but my husband received several.
-Several members we spoke to said they had been members for 10+ years but were increasingly annoyed about membership over the last year or so (decline in quality of people and a high turn over in staff).

We liked the fitness areas an amenities, but we'll probably wait for a year or so and see if the overall moral and cleanliness of locker rooms improves before we buy a membership. The Goleta location is too much out of our way for a daily trek.< /review>
